First View: Karama Not by Choice
Sanusi reports the first alternative distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first distinction between mu'jiza and karama based on the saint's intention.

Core Idea
Karama occurs without the saint's intention, unlike a miracle.

Sanusi begins by presenting a view from some imams that the key difference is intentionality. A miracle happens by the prophet's choice, but a karama does not. Let's examine this opinion and its clarification of terms.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation to get the gist of the first view.
Notice the terms 'ikhtiyar' and 'irada'.
2
Understand the distinction
Identify that the view states karama does not occur by the saint's choice or intention, unlike a miracle.
3
Clarify the terms
Learn that 'choice' here means desire and longing, because the supernormal act may be beyond the servant's power.
The author explains the ambiguity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومِنْ أَئِمَّتِنا مَنْ ذهب إلى أنَّ الفرق بينهما : أنَّ الكرامة لا تقع على اختيار وقصدِ مِنَ الوليّ بخلافِ المعجزة ، والمراد بالاختيار والإرادة هنا : الشهوة والتمني ؛ إذ الفعلُ الخارقُ قد يكونُ مِنْ غيرِ جنسِ مقدور العبد و مرادِه . ومِنَ الأئمَّةِ مَنْ فَرَّقَ بينهما : بأنَّ كلَّ ما وقع مِنَ الخوارقِ معجزة لنبي لا يقع كرامة لولي ؛ كإحياء الموتى ، وإبراء الأكمه ، وقلب العصا حيَّةً ، وفلقِ البحر أطواداً على يد الأولياء، والأستاذُ يُصرِّحُ بمنع هذا ومنع غيرِهِ مِنَ الخوارقِ على يدِ الأولياء، وإِنَّما يُجوِّزُ ما يجري مجرى إجابة الدعوةِ ، ووجودِ ماء في البريَّة ، وغيرِ ذلكَ ممَّا يُكرِمُ الله تعالى بهِ عبادَهُ ولا يبلغ خوارق العاداتِ .
And among our imams there is one who held that the difference between them is that the charismatic wonder does not occur by choice and intention of the saint, unlike the miracle. And by choice and will here is meant desire and longing; for the supernormal act may be of a different genus from what is within the servant's power and will. And among the imams there is one who distinguished between them by saying that every supernormal event that occurs as a miracle for a prophet cannot occur as a charismatic wonder for a saint, such as raising the dead, curing the blind from birth, turning a staff into a snake, and splitting the sea into mountains at the hands of saints. And the Ustadh explicitly forbids this and forbids other supernormal events at the hands of saints; he only permits what follows the course of answering a prayer, the appearance of water in the desert, and other things by which God honors His servants and which do not reach the level of supernormal events.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage presents two alternative views on the distinction between mu'jiza and karama, and then the restrictive position of al-Ustadh (al-Isfarayini). The first view states that a karama does not occur by the saint's choice or intention, unlike a miracle; 'choice' here means desire and wish, because the supernormal act may be of a different type from what the servant can ordinarily produce. The second view states that certain supernormal events (like raising the dead, healing the blind, the staff turning into a snake, splitting the sea) are exclusive to prophets and cannot occur as karamat for saints. Then al-Ustadh prohibits both these views and denies all supernormal events at the hands of saints; he only allows events like answered prayers or finding water in the desert, which are not truly 'supernormal' (khariq li'l-ada).

Key Terms
اختيار
إرادة
شهوة
تمني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that saints can perform karamat by their own will and intention.
Correction: This view teaches that karamat do not occur by the saint's choice; they are not intended or sought.

Checkpoint
According to the first view, what is the difference between a miracle and a karama?
A) A karama occurs by the saint's choice, a miracle does not.
B) A miracle occurs by the prophet's choice, a karama does not.
C) Both occur by choice.
D) Neither occurs by choice.

Key Takeaway
The first view distinguishes mu'jiza and karama by the presence of intentionality: miracles are willed, karamat are not.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever received a blessing that you did not seek or intend? How did you feel when you realized it was a pure gift from Allah, not from your own effort? This lesson teaches that karamat come without the saint's intention. Can you recall a specific blessing in your life that you did not ask for? Write it down and consciously thank Allah for it today.
?
The passage clarifies that 'choice' here means desire and longing. Think of a time when you strongly desired something good but it was beyond your power. Did you still try to achieve it, or did you rely on Allah? How does this lesson help you understand that not every good thing comes from your own intention? What is one area of your life where you need to trust Allah's gift rather than your own planning?
?
Consider the difference between something you intentionally strive for and something that comes to you without your effort. In your spiritual life, which matters more? The saint does not seek the karama; it is a sign from Allah. Are you seeking signs from Allah, or are you focused on obedience? Ask yourself: Do I ever try to force spiritual experiences? What can I learn from the saint's receptivity and lack of personal ambition in this matter?

Second View: Exclusive Miracles
Sanusi reports the second alternative distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second distinction that certain supernormal events are exclusive to prophets and cannot occur as karamat.

Core Idea
Some miracles are prophet-only; saints cannot replicate them.

The second view from another group of imams takes a different approach: it lists specific supernormal events that are reserved for prophets. Let's see which events are considered exclusive and why.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the second view.
Notice the examples given.
2
Identify the rule
The view states that any supernormal event that occurs as a miracle for a prophet cannot happen as a karama for a saint.
3
Study the examples
Learn the examples: raising the dead, curing the blind, turning the staff into a snake, splitting the sea.
These are classic prophetic miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

This passage presents two alternative views on the distinction between mu'jiza and karama, and then the restrictive position of al-Ustadh (al-Isfarayini). The first view states that a karama does not occur by the saint's choice or intention, unlike a miracle; 'choice' here means desire and wish, because the supernormal act may be of a different type from what the servant can ordinarily produce. Ustadh's Denial of Karamat
Sanusi reports the ustadh's restrictive position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ustadh's position that denies all supernormal events at the hands of saints, except for minor favors.

Core Idea
The ustadh rejects karamat altogether, allowing only everyday kindnesses.

Having presented two views, Sanusi now reports the strict position of al-Ustadh (al-Isfarayini). He forbids both the claim that certain miracles are exclusive and any supernormal event for saints. Let's see what he permits instead.

Guided Path
1
Read the ustadh's statement
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the firm denial.
Note the word 'yusarrihu' indicating explicit forbiddance.
2
Understand what is forbidden
The ustadh forbids both the second view (exclusive miracles) and all other supernormal events at the hands of saints.
3
Learn what is allowed
He only permits events like answered prayers, finding water, etc. — things that do not break natural laws.
These are not considered khariq li'l-ada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومِنْ أَئِمَّتِنا مَنْ ذهب إلى أنَّ الفرق بينهما : أنَّ الكرامة لا تقع على اختيار وقصدِ مِنَ الوليّ بخلافِ المعجزة ، والمراد بالاختيار والإرادة هنا : الشهوة والتمني ؛ إذ الفعلُ الخارقُ قد يكونُ مِنْ غيرِ جنسِ مقدور العبد و مرادِه . ومِنَ الأئمَّةِ مَنْ فَرَّقَ بينهما : بأنَّ كلَّ ما وقع مِنَ الخوارقِ معجزة لنبي لا يقع كرامة لولي ؛ كإحياء الموتى ، وإبراء الأكمه ، وقلب العصا حيَّةً ، وفلقِ البحر أطواداً على يد الأولياء، والأستاذُ يُصرِّحُ بمنع هذا ومنع غيرِهِ مِنَ الخوارقِ على يدِ الأولياء، وإِنَّما يُجوِّزُ ما يجري مجرى إجابة الدعوةِ ، ووجودِ ماء في البريَّة ، وغيرِ ذلكَ ممَّا يُكرِمُ الله تعالى بهِ عبادَهُ ولا يبلغ خوارق العاداتِ .
And among our imams there is one who held that the difference between them is that the charismatic wonder does not occur by choice and intention of the saint, unlike the miracle. And by choice and will here is meant desire and longing; for the supernormal act may be of a different genus from what is within the servant's power and will. And among the imams there is one who distinguished between them by saying that every supernormal event that occurs as a miracle for a prophet cannot occur as a charismatic wonder for a saint, such as raising the dead, curing the blind from birth, turning a staff into a snake, and splitting the sea into mountains at the hands of saints. And the Ustadh explicitly forbids this and forbids other supernormal events at the hands of saints; he only permits what follows the course of answering a prayer, the appearance of water in the desert, and other things by which God honors His servants and which do not reach the level of supernormal events.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage presents two alternative views on the distinction between mu'jiza and karama, and then the restrictive position of al-Ustadh (al-Isfarayini). The first view states that a karama does not occur by the saint's choice or intention, unlike a miracle; 'choice' here means desire and wish, because the supernormal act may be of a different type from what the servant can ordinarily produce. The second view states that certain supernormal events (like raising the dead, healing the blind, the staff turning into a snake, splitting the sea) are exclusive to prophets and cannot occur as karamat for saints. Then al-Ustadh prohibits both these views and denies all supernormal events at the hands of saints; he only allows events like answered prayers or finding water in the desert, which are not truly 'supernormal' (khariq li'l-ada).

Key Terms
خوارق العادات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume all scholars accept karamat; the ustadh's view is a minority position that denies them.
Correction: Al-Ustadh denies all supernormal events for saints, allowing only ordinary favors.

Checkpoint
What does the ustadh permit as a favor for saints?
A) Raising the dead
B) Splitting the sea
C) Answered prayers
D) Turning a staff into a snake

Key Takeaway
The ustadh denies all supernormal events for saints, allowing only ordinary divine favors.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you are a saint, do you need supernormal events to prove your closeness to God? Or is the simple answer to prayer enough? How does this lesson challenge your desire for visible signs of God's love?
?
The Ustadh allows only ordinary divine favors like finding water in the desert. Think of a time God answered a small, ordinary prayer for you. Did you consider it a sign of His love, or did you expect something more dramatic? What does this teach you about humility in seeking God?
?
This lesson reveals a scholar who said, 'No supernormal events for saints.' If you heard this view before, would you have rejected it as too restrictive? Are you willing to accept that God's kindness in everyday life is sufficient proof of His friendship, even without miracles? What would change in your spiritual life if you truly believed that?

Refutation of the Objection from the Prophet's Challenge
Sanusi refutes an objection and states the verifiers' position on karamat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's challenge does not prevent karamat from occurring at the hands of saints, and the distinction between miracles and karamat according to the verifiers.

Core Idea
The Prophet's challenge is qualified and does not prevent karamat; rather, karamat support prophethood.

Sanusi addresses a common objection that the Prophet's unique challenge would preclude any similar supernormal event from a saint. He refutes this by showing the challenge is limited to opponents and liars, and then presents the consensus of the verifiers that karamat are permissible and actually reinforce the prophet's truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Note the structure: objection, refutation, and conclusion.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the objection
Find the claim that the Prophet's statement prevents karamat. Notice how it is presented as a potential problem.
3
Understand the refutation
See how Sanusi refutes by qualifying the challenge: it only applies to opponents and liars, not followers. Also note the consensus support.
The refutation uses the example of another prophet.
4
Learn the verifiers' position
Grasp the final doctrine: all supernormal events are possible for saints, and the difference from miracles is the claim of prophethood.
Karamat are a blessing of following the prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهؤلاء يزعمونَ أنَّ قولَ النبي : ( لا يأتي أحدٌ بمثل ما أتيتُ بهِ ) يمنعُ مِنْ وقوع شيءٍ مِنْ معجزاتِ الأنبياء على أيدي الأولياء ؛ لئلا يؤدِّيَ إلى تكذيب مَنْ ثبت صدقُهُ ، وهذا مُندِفعُ ؛ فإنَّ تحدِّيَ النبي مُقيَّدٌ بأنَّهُ لا يظهرُ ما أتى بهِ على يدِ مَنْ يبغي معارضته ومناقضته ، ولا على يد مفترِ كذَّابٍ ، ويدلُّ على هذا التقييدِ : أَنَّ ظهور ما أتى بهِ على يد نبي آخر لا يقدح في معجزته اتفاقاً . ومذهبُ المُحققينَ : جوازُ وقوع الخوارق كلها على يد الولي باختياره وبغير اختيارِهِ ، وأنَّ الفرق بينها وبين المعجزة ما قدمناه أولاً مِنْ دعوى النبوَّة وعدمها ، والولي إنَّما يظهرُ عَلَى يَدِهِ ما يظهرُ مِنَ الكراماتِ ببركة متابعته للرسول والاقتداء به ، فهو أحق بالدلالة على صدْقِ المتبوع وعاضد لهُ
And these people claim that the Prophet's saying: 'No one will come with what I have brought' prevents the occurrence of any of the prophets' miracles at the hands of saints, lest it lead to the discrediting of one whose truthfulness is established. But this is refutable; for the Prophet's challenge is qualified: what he brought does not appear at the hand of one who seeks to oppose and contradict him, nor at the hand of a lying fabricator. And this qualification is supported by the fact that the appearance of what he brought at the hand of another prophet does not detract from his miracle by consensus. And the doctrine of the verifiers is: the permissibility of all supernormal events occurring at the hand of the saint, by his choice or without his choice, and that the difference between them and the miracle is what we first mentioned: the claim of prophethood and its absence. And the saint only causes to appear what appears of charismatic wonders by the blessing of his following the messenger and his imitation of him; thus it is more deserving of indicating the truth of the followed one and is a supporter for him.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its refutation, then states the position of the verifiers (muhqaqiqun). The objectors argue that the Prophet's statement 'No one will come with what I have brought' (implying uniqueness) prevents any supernormal event similar to his miracles from occurring at the hands of saints, because that would imply someone else can do what he did, thus discrediting him. The refutation is that the Prophet's challenge is qualified: it only prohibits appearance on someone opposing him or a lying claimant, not on a saint who follows him. Consensus confirms that if another prophet produced the same miracle, it would not detract from the original prophet's miracle. The verifiers therefore hold that all supernormal events are possible for saints, and the only difference is the presence or absence of a claim to prophethood. The saint's karamat actually strengthen the prophet's truth because they stem from following him.

Key Terms
تحدي
مقيد
معارضة
مفتر كذاب
مذهب المحققين
بركة متابعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Prophet's challenge absolutely prevents any similar supernormal event from occurring at the hands of anyone.
Correction: The challenge is qualified: it only prevents appearance on an opponent or a liar, not on a saint who follows the prophet.

Checkpoint
According to the refutation, why does the appearance of a miracle-like event at the hand of a saint not discredit the Prophet?
A) Because the saint is a follower, not an opponent or liar.
B) Because the saint's event is weaker.
C) Because the Prophet's challenge was only for his own time.
D) Because saints are infallible like prophets.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's challenge is qualified; karamat are permissible and actually support the truth of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you follow the Prophet sincerely enough that your life could be described as a 'blessing of following'? What specific habits or attitudes need to change for your actions to reflect that following?
?
When you see or hear of supernatural events attributed to pious people, do you ever doubt the finality of prophethood? How does this lesson's distinction between miracle and karamah challenge or reassure you?
?
The saint's karamah is a support for the truth of the prophet. Is your own life a support for the truth of Islam? If not, what is one concrete step you can take today to make your actions more aligned with the Prophet's teachings?

Distinguishing Karama from Sihr and Defining Karama
Sanusi distinguishes karama from sihr and defines karama.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi distinguishes karama from sihr based on the moral status of the agent and defines karama as a supernormal event not linked to prophethood.

Core Idea
Karama is a wonder of the righteous; sihr is a wonder of the wicked.

This passage from Sanusi clarifies an important theological distinction: the difference between the charismatic wonders (karamat) granted to saints and the deceptive sorcery (sihr) of disbelievers and sinners. It also provides a precise definition of karama that distinguishes it from a prophet's miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice that the passage has two clear parts: a distinction and a definition.
The passage uses a bracket as a subheading: [حد الكرامة]
2
Identify the distinction
Find the key difference between karama and sihr: the condition of the person through whom the supernormal event appears (righteous vs. disbeliever/sinner).
Focus on the phrase 'بخلاف السحر'
3
Analyze the definition
Examine the definition of karama: it has three components—supernormal event, righteous servant, and not a prophet (now or later). Consider why each component is necessary.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Think about why this distinction matters in aqeedah. It protects the status of prophets (mu'jiza) and prevents confusion between genuine sainthood and sorcery.
This connects to the broader discussion of miracles in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الفرقُ بين الكرامة والسحر : فهو أنَّ الكرامة ظهور الخارقِ على يد عبد ظاهرِ الصلاح ، بخلافِ السحرِ ؛ فإنَّ الخارق فيهِ إِنَّما يظهر على أيدي الكفرةِ والفُسَّاقِ [ حد الكرامة ] وحدَّ بعضُهم الكرامة فقالَ : هي عبارة عن ظهور خارق للعادة على يد عبدِ ظاهرِ الصلاحِ ليسَ بنبي في الحالِ ولا في المآلِ
And as for the difference between the charismatic wonder and sorcery: it is that the charismatic wonder is the appearance of the supernormal at the hand of a servant outwardly righteous, unlike sorcery; for the supernormal in it only appears at the hands of disbelievers and sinners. [Definition of the charismatic wonder] And some defined the charismatic wonder, saying: it is an expression for the appearance of a supernormal event at the hand of a servant outwardly righteous, who is not a prophet at present nor in the future.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage gives two related pieces: first, the distinction between karama and sihr (sorcery). The karama appears at the hand of a righteous servant (one who is outwardly pious and presumably a saint), while sihr appears at the hands of disbelievers and sinners. Second, it provides a formal definition of karama: a supernormal event that appears at the hand of a servant who is outwardly righteous and who is not a prophet at the present time nor will become a prophet in the future (i.e., he is not a prophet in any sense). This definition distinguishes karama from both mu'jiza (which is linked to prophethood) and sihr (which is linked to evil people).

Key Terms
سحر
صلاح
كفرة
فساق
حد الكرامة
في الحال
في المآل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think karama and sihr are the same phenomenon with different names.
Correction: Karama is distinguished by the righteousness of the agent and the absence of prophethood; sihr is associated with disbelief and sin.

Checkpoint
How is a karama distinguished from sihr according to the passage?
A) Karama is more powerful.
B) Karama appears through a righteous person, sihr through disbelievers or sinners.
C) Karama involves supernatural beings, sihr does not.
D) Karama is always miraculous, sihr is illusion.

Key Takeaway
Karama is a supernormal event performed by a righteous non-prophet, while sihr is performed by disbelievers or sinners.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness an extraordinary event in someone's life, do you immediately attribute it to Allah or are you tempted to think the person has some special power? How does this lesson's clear distinction between karama (from Allah for the righteous) and sihr (from evil) challenge your default assumptions? Commit today to always trace every wonder back to Allah alone, and to judge people's spiritual state not by their miracles but by their obedience.
?
This lesson defines karama as appearing through someone 'outwardly righteous.' Look at your own life: are you more concerned with appearing righteous to others, or with being truly righteous before Allah? Where do you fall short in sincerity? Determine one specific area this week where you will work on internal sincerity rather than external show.
?
The definition of karama excludes prophets, emphasizing that the highest miracles belong to the Prophets. Do your own heart and actions reflect proper reverence for the Prophets, especially Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him)? Or do you sometimes elevate righteous people to a status that only Prophets deserve? Repent of any excess and recommit to following the Prophetic sunna with humility.

Two Jewish Sects That Denied Muhammad's Prophethood
Sanusi describes two Jewish sects that rejected Muhammad and their arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two Jewish sects' objections to Muhammad's prophethood and the theological assumptions behind them.

Core Idea
The first sect rejected Muhammad over abrogation; the second accepted him only for Arabs.

Sanusi presents two actual historical Jewish responses to Islam. The first group denied Muhammad's prophethood entirely because his law abrogated parts of the Torah, which they considered impossible. The second group, the 'Īsawiyya, acknowledged him as a prophet but restricted his mission to Arabs, thereby exempting themselves. This passage prepares us to understand their refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice how Sanusi concisely presents each sect and their reasoning.
The passage uses technical terms like naskh (abrogation) and badā' (change of mind).
2
Identify the two sects and their positions
The first sect is unnamed but rejects prophethood due to abrogation. The second is named 'Īsawiyya and accepts Muhammad but only for Arabs. Pay attention to their distinct arguments.
3
Analyze the arguments of the first sect
They have two arguments: 1) abrogation implies badā' in God, which they deem impossible; 2) a transmitted report (naql) that Moses said his law is eternal and to keep the Sabbath forever.
The second argument is scriptural, the first is rational.
4
Understand the second sect's position
The 'Īsawiyya do not deny Muhammad's prophethood but limit his mission. This implies they are not obligated to follow him, which is a form of rejection for non-Arabs.
5
Reflect on the underlying assumptions
Consider why abrogation was seen as problematic. The assumption that naskh implies badā' is a key theological issue, which later refutations will address.
This connects to the common misunderstanding about God's knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرقة امتنعتْ مِنْ تصديقِهِ : لما تضمَّنَتُهُ شريعتُهُ مِنْ نَسْخِ بعضِ أحكام شريعة موسى صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، وزعموا أنَّ النسخ محال ، وتمسكوا في إحالته على أنَّ النسْخَ يستلزمُ البَداء ، وبعضُهم تمسَّكَ في إحالته على النقل فقالوا : إنَّ موسى عليه الصلاةُ والسلام نص على أنَّ شريعتَهُ لا تُنسَخُ ، وأَنَّهُ قالَ : تمسكوا بالسبتِ أبداً. الفرقة الثانيةُ : تُعرَفُ بالعيسويَّةِ ، قالوا : محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام رسول ، لكن إلى العرب خاصةً.
A group refrained from believing him because his law contained abrogation of some rulings of the law of Moses, peace be upon him, and they claimed that abrogation is impossible. They adhered to its impossibility on the grounds that abrogation implies badā' (change of mind), and some of them adhered to its impossibility on the basis of transmission (naql), saying: Moses, peace be upon him, explicitly stated that his law cannot be abrogated, and that he said: 'Hold fast to the Sabbath forever.' The second group is known as the 'Īsawiyya; they said: Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, is a messenger, but only to the Arabs specifically.
Source pages p. 577

Commentary
This passage identifies and characterizes two Jewish groups that denied the prophethood of Muhammad. The first group refused to believe because Muhammad's law abrogated some laws of the Torah. They considered abrogation (naskh) impossible, and they had two arguments: first, that abrogation implies badā' (God changing His mind), which they considered unfit for God; second, based on transmitted texts, they claimed that Moses explicitly stated that his law is eternal and specifically commanded keeping the Sabbath forever. The second group, the 'Īsawiyya, accepted Muhammad as a prophet but limited his mission to Arabs, implying that they themselves were not obligated to follow him. The author presents these views before refuting them in the following passages.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh)
بداء (badā')
عيسوية ('Īsawiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abrogation implies that God changes His mind (badā'), which would be a defect in God.
Correction: The passage shows this Jewish assumption, but Islamic theology holds that abrogation is a legitimate exercise of God's will and does not imply ignorance or change of mind; it is part of divine wisdom.

Checkpoint
What was the main reason the first Jewish group refused to believe in Muhammad according to this passage?
A) They thought Muhammad was not a prophet at all.
B) They believed Muhammad's law abrogated some laws of Moses.
C) They thought Muhammad was only for Arabs.
D) They rejected miracles.

Key Takeaway
The passage presents two Jewish objections: one based on the impossibility of abrogation of the Torah, and another that accepts Muhammad's prophethood but restricts it to Arabs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The first group rejected the truth because it contradicted their prior beliefs. Are there any truths about Islam that you have resisted because they challenge your comfortable assumptions? What will you do about that resistance starting today?
?
The 'Īsawiyya accepted Muhammad as a prophet but limited his message to others, exempting themselves. Do you ever selectively apply Islamic teachings to others while excusing yourself? Which command are you currently rationalizing away as 'not for you'?
?
Both groups relied on arguments that seemed strong to them but were false. When you study aqeedah, do you seek to defend your own views or to submit to the truth wherever it leads? Commit to one change in how you approach learning from now on.

Evidence from the Torah: Abrogation in Jewish Law
Sanusi proves that naskh is present in the Torah itself with examples from Noah and Adam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that abrogation (naskh) is not unique to Islam but is also present in the Torah, as demonstrated by examples from Noah and Adam.

Core Idea
Abrogation is a universal divine pattern, not an Islamic innovation.

Sanusi now turns the tables on those who reject abrogation in Islam while accepting the Torah. He points to two clear examples from the Torah itself—changes in dietary laws after Noah and the prohibition of sibling marriage after Adam—to show that abrogation is intrinsic to God's revealed law. This passage sets the stage for a broader defense of naskh as a rational and scriptural necessity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once for its flow, then read the literal translation. Notice the two distinct examples Sanusi cites.
The passage is concise but dense with scriptural reference.
2
Identify the two examples of abrogation
Find the example from Noah's law (permission of all foods except blood, later restricted) and from Adam's law (permission of sister marriage, later forbidden). See how each shows a change in divine ruling.
3
Reflect on the argument's force
Ask yourself: Why is this a strong rebuttal? Because it uses the opponent's own scripture to prove that abrogation is not an innovation. This is a common method in theological debates.
Sanusi is using a 'proof from within' the Torah itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النسخ : فهو لازمٌ في شرعهم أيضاً ; إذْ قد ثبتَ مِنْ نص التوراة أنَّ الله تعالى قد قالَ لنوحٍ حينَ خرجَ مِنَ السفينة : ( إِنِّي جاعل كل دابَّةٍ مأكلاً لكَ ولذريَّتِكَ , وأطلقتُ ذلك لكم كسائر العشب ما خلا الدم ) , وقد حُرِّمَ بعد ذلك في التوراة أشياء كثيرة , وفي التوراة : أنَّ مِنْ شريعةِ آدمَ عليه السلام جواز نكاح الأختِ , وقد حُرَّموا ذلكَ
And as for abrogation, it is also necessary in their law; for it has been established from the text of the Torah that God, exalted, said to Noah when he came out of the ark: 'I am making every creature a food for you and your descendants, and I have permitted that to you like the green herbs, except blood.' Then after that, many things were forbidden in the Torah. And in the Torah, it is stated that from the law of Adam, peace be upon him, marrying one's sister was permissible, but they forbade that.
Source pages p. 578

Commentary
This passage provides empirical evidence from the Torah itself that abrogation (naskh) occurs within Jewish law. Sanusi gives two examples: first, after Noah's flood, God permitted all animals as food except blood, but later many foods were forbidden in the Mosaic law, showing a change in permitted food. Second, in Adam's law, marriage to one's sister was permissible, but later Jewish law forbade it. These examples demonstrate that the Jews cannot consistently object to abrogation in Islam while accepting it in their own tradition.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh)
توراة (Torah)
نوح (Noah)
آدم (Adam)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think abrogation is unique to Islam and therefore suspect.
Correction: Abrogation existed in previous revelations, as shown by examples from the Torah.

Checkpoint
Which example does Sanusi give to show abrogation in the Torah?
A) The prohibition of pork.
B) Permission of all foods for Noah except blood, then later restrictions.
C) The ten commandments.
D) The story of Moses and Pharaoh.

Key Takeaway
Abrogation is a consistent divine practice, as evidenced by changes in dietary and marriage laws within the Torah itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's law could change from Noah to Moses, what does that say about your own assumptions that Islamic rulings are static? Have you ever dismissed a difficult command by thinking it is outdated? What would it take for you to submit to a ruling that goes against your desires?
?
The Torah explicitly permitted what later became forbidden. How does that challenge your view of previous scriptures? Are you willing to study them with an open heart to see God's hand, or do you dismiss them outright?
?
Sanusi uses the Jews' own scripture to prove naskh. If someone today uses the Quran to argue against you, would you be humble enough to re-examine your position? What are you holding onto that you think is absolute but might need to be revised for your spiritual growth?

Refuting the Objection on Divergent Views of I'jaz
Sanusi answers the objection that disagreement on the aspect of i'jaz undermines the miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the objection that scholarly disagreement on the aspect of the Quran's miraculousness undermines its miracle.

Core Idea
The miracle of the Quran is its challenge being unmet, not the explanation of why.

A common objection against the Quranic miracle is that scholars disagree on what makes it miraculous. If they cannot agree, how can it be a clear miracle? Sanusi addresses this by distinguishing between the undeniable fact of the miracle and the theoretical debate about its cause. In this passage, he provides a crisp refutation that protects the doctrine from skepticism.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objection claims that disagreement among scholars on the aspect of i'jaz invalidates the miracle because a miracle must be clear. Read the objector's argument and note the three positions mentioned: composition, eloquence, and sarf.
The objector lists three views: some say it's only composition, some only eloquence, some say it's sarf (divine turning away).
2
Identify Sanusi's answer
Sanusi responds by separating the fact of the miracle from its explanation. Notice his key move: the inability of creation to oppose the Quran is known and undisputed.
He states that 'the inability of creation to oppose it with a surah like it is known and manifest, not doubted at all.'
3
Reflect on the distinction
Understand why disagreement on the cause does not affect the reality of the miracle. This is a critical logical move in kalam.
The disagreement is only about 'realizing the aspect from which the miracle came,' not about the miracle itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد اعترض بعض أهل الزيغ والضلال على معجزة القرآن فقالوا: إنكم زعمتم أن وجه إعجازه فصاحته وجزالته، ونظمه وبلاغته، ثم اختلفتم اختلافاً كثيراً على ما نقلتموه من تفاصيل الأقوال في ذلك، فإن من يزعم أن ذلك هو النظم فقط فقد أنكر كون الفصاحة والجزالة فيه معجزاً، وبالعكس، ومن زعم أنه الصرف فقد أنكر الوجهين جميعاً، ومن قال بغير الصرف فقد أنكر كون الصرف معجزاً، وحق المعجزة أن تكون ظاهرة للكل بحيث لا يستراب فيها ألبتة. والجواب: أن عجز الخلق عن معارضته بسورة من مثله معلوم ظاهر لا يستراب فيه ألبتة، ولم يختلف فيه أحد، وبهذا يعرف كونه معجزة، والاختلاف بعد ذلك في وجه إعجازه لا يقتضي الخلاف في كونه معجزة ولا في عدم ظهور ذلك، وإنما خلاف هو في تحقيق الوجه الذي جاء منه الإعجاز، وقد بينا في أصل العقيدة عجز البلغاء عن معارضته بياناً شافياً لا يحتاج إلى شرح.
And some people of error and misguidance objected to the miracle of the Quran, saying: You claimed that the aspect of its miraculousness is its eloquence and fluency, its composition and rhetoric, then you disagreed greatly according to what you have transmitted of details of opinions on that. For whoever claims that it is only the composition has denied that eloquence and fluency are miraculous in it, and vice versa. And whoever claims that it is the turning away (sarf) has denied both aspects, and whoever says other than sarf has denied that sarf is miraculous. And the right of a miracle is that it be manifest to all such that it is never doubted. The answer: That the inability of creation to oppose it with a surah like it is known and manifest, not doubted at all, and no one has disagreed about it. And by this it is known that it is a miracle. Disagreement after that about the aspect of its miraculousness does not entail disagreement about it being a miracle nor about its lack of appearance. Rather it is disagreement in realizing the aspect from which the miracle came. And we have explained in the original creed the inability of eloquent people to oppose it with a sufficient explanation that needs no commentary.
Source pages p. 586

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objectors argue that since scholars disagree on what aspect of the Quran constitutes its miracle (some say composition, some eloquence, some sarf), then the miracle is not clear and thus invalid. The answer is that the fact of the challenge being unmet is undisputed and clear to all; the disagreement is only about the precise cause of that inability. The miracle itself is known by the inability to produce similar speech, not by the theoretical explanation. The author asserts that he has already explained this in his original creed.

إعجاز
فصاحة
جزالة
نظم
بلاغة
صرف
معجزة
عجز الخلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Disagreement among scholars about the aspect of i'jaz proves the Quran is not a miracle.
Correction: The miracle is the inability to produce similar speech, which is universally accepted; disagreement only concerns the explanation of that inability.

Checkpoint
What is the core answer to the objection that disagreement on the aspect of i'jaz weakens the Quranic miracle?
A) The disagreement proves the miracle is stronger.
B) The miracle is the inability to produce similar speech, which is universally accepted.
C) The objectors are not qualified to judge.
D) The Quran's miracle is not based on eloquence.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's miraculousness is proven by the universal inability to produce a similar surah, regardless of differing theories about its cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever allowed doubts to creep in because you heard scholars disagree on a matter of faith? How does this lesson challenge you to separate the undeniable fact from competing explanations? What will you do the next time such a doubt arises?
?
The objectors argued that a miracle must be 'manifest to all such that it is never doubted.' Look at your own heart: is the Quran's miraculousness as clear to you as the inability of anyone to produce its like? If not, what is blocking that certainty, and what step will you take today to remove it?
?
Sanusi points to the universal inability of creation as the proof. Do you rely on this proof in your own conviction, or do you lean on secondary arguments that could be debated? Which of your beliefs are built on indisputable foundations, and which are built on speculation? Commit to reinforcing one foundation this week.

Sanusi's Refutation of the Batiniyya
Sanusi refutes the Batiniyya claim that threats are only for intimidation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi refutes the Batiniyya claim that divine threats are only for intimidation, and how he counters their arguments using scripture and reason.

Core Idea
Divine threats are real; God's justice is not bound by human reasoning.

In this passage, Sanusi tackles a serious theological error: the belief that God's threats of punishment are merely rhetorical. The Batiniyya sect held this view, arguing from God's mercy and predestination. Sanusi systematically refutes them, exposing the flaws in their reasoning and the dangers of delving into the secrets of qadar.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Batiniyya position
Read the opening lines to grasp the Batiniyya claim that Quranic threats are only for intimidation, not actual punishment.
Notice that Sanusi presents this as the first of three schools.
2
Examine their first argument
They cite Q. 39:16. Sanusi points out that the verse refers to worldly intimidation, not the afterlife.
This is a key scriptural refutation.
3
Examine their second and third arguments
They argue from God's mercy and from predestination. Sanusi dismisses these as based on false reasoning (al-tahsin al-aqli) and forbidden inquiry into qadar.
He cites a hadith to support his position.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Sanusi affirms that Allah does as He wills, and we have no knowledge except what He teaches us.
This reinforces the limits of human reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم : أَنَّ نفوذ الوعيدِ اختلفَ الناسُ فيهِ على ثلاثةِ مذاهب : الأول : أنَّ الوعيدَ الوارد في الكتب الإلهيَّةِ إِنَّما جاءَ للتخويف فقط، وأمَّا فعلُ الإيلام فلا ! وهذا قولُ الباطنيّة ، واحتجوا بقوله تعالى : ذَلِكَ يُخَوِّفُ اللهُ بِهِ عِبَادَهُ ﴾ [الزمر : ١٦] ، ولا يخفى فساده ؛ فإِنَّ التخويف المذكور في الآيةِ إنَّما هو في الدنيا ، وفي الآخرة يقعُ المخوَّفُ بهِ . واحتجوا أيضاً : بأنَّ الحكيم أرحم الراحمين ؛ كيف يُعذِّبُ حيواناً ضعيفاً غايتُهُ أنَّهُ بمعصيتِهِ إِنَّما قصَّرَ في حق نفسِهِ ؛ لاستحالة أنْ يكونَ الله تعالى نفع في عمل أحد أو ضرر به ؟! س وأيضاً : فالأفعالُ كلُّها واقعة بإرادتِهِ تعالى وخلقِهِ ، لا أثر للعبدِ في شيء منها ! وهذا الكلامُ منهم مبني على التحسين العقلي ، وهو باطل ، وعلى طلب الاطلاع على سرَّ القَدَرِ ، وهو ممَّا نُهينا عن الخوض فيهِ ، قالَ رسولُ اللهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : « إِذَا ذُكِرَ الْقَدَرُ فَأَمْسِكُوا (١) ، والله سبحانَهُ يفعل ما يشاء ، ويحكم ما يريد ، ولا علم لنا بشيءٍ إِلا أَنْ يُعلِّمَنا جلَّ وعزَّ .
Know: The execution of the threat has been differed upon by people into three schools. The first: that the threat mentioned in the divine books came only for intimidation, not for actual infliction of pain! This is the saying of the Batiniyya. They argued by His saying: 'That is how Allah warns His servants' (Q. 39:16), but its corruption is not hidden, for the intimidation mentioned in the verse is only in the world, and in the afterlife the threatened thing occurs. They also argued: The Wise One is the Most Merciful of the merciful; how can He punish a weak animal whose utmost is that he by his disobedience only fell short in his own right? Because it is impossible that Allah benefits or harms in anyone's action?! And also: All actions occur by His will and creation; the servant has no effect in any of them! This speech of theirs is built upon rational tashbih (al-tahsin al-aqli), which is false, and upon seeking insight into the secret of qadar, which is something we have been forbidden to delve into. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When qadar is mentioned, refrain.' And Allah the Exalted does as He wills and judges as He wants, and we have no knowledge of anything unless He teaches us, Exalted and Glorified.
Source pages p. 628

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the first of three schools on the execution of divine threat. Sanusi begins by stating that the first school, that of the Batiniyya (an esoteric sect), claims that Quranic threats of punishment are merely for intimidation and will not actually occur. He then examines their three arguments. First, they cite Q. 39:16, but Sanusi points out that the intimidation mentioned there is worldly, while the threatened punishment will occur in the Hereafter. Second, they argue from God's mercy: a merciful God would not punish a weak creature. Sanusi dismisses this as based on rationalist reasoning (التحسين العقلي), which is false. Third, they argue from divine predetermination: since all actions are by God's will and creation, humans have no role, so punishment would be unjust. Sanusi labels this as forbidden inquiry into qadar (divine decree) and cites a hadith commanding silence when qadar is discussed. He concludes by affirming God's absolute freedom and our limited knowledge, thereby rejecting the Batiniyya's position.

Key Terms
نفوذ الوعيد
الباطنية
التحسين العقلي
القدر
التخويف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Batiniyya believed that God's threats of punishment are only for intimidation and will not actually be carried out.
Correction: Sanusi refutes this by showing that the Quranic verses about intimidation refer to worldly matters, and that God's justice and mercy do not contradict His actual punishment of sinners. He also warns against rationalist reasoning and delving into qadar.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, the Batiniyya's argument that all actions are by God's will leads them to deny the execution of the threat. Which type of reasoning does he say it is based on?
A) Logical syllogism
B) Rational tashbih (al-tahsin al-aqli)
C) Scriptural evidence
D) Consensus

Key Takeaway
Sanusi firmly rejects the Batiniyya's denial of actual punishment by exposing the flaws in their arguments and reminding us to rely on revelation, not rational speculation, in matters of divine decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you ever downplay its seriousness by thinking, 'God is merciful, He'll forgive me anyway'? How does the Batiniyya's error of reducing threats to mere intimidation mirror your own heart's tendency to avoid the fear of punishment? What tangible action can you take today to remind yourself that divine warnings are real?
?
Have you ever caught yourself demanding that God's actions fit your sense of fairness—questioning why He allows suffering or why He would punish certain people? How does the lesson's rejection of rational tashbih challenge your own desire to make God fit your standards? Will you submit to His will even when it confuses you?
?
Do you instinctively shy away from thinking about death and judgment because it feels uncomfortable? The Batiniyya tried to remove that discomfort by denying the reality of punishment. Where in your life have you tried to 'soften' the teachings of Islam to avoid feeling accountable? What is one specific teaching you have been avoiding that you now commit to facing?

The Murji'a Claim: Punishment Only for Disbelievers
Sanusi presents the Murji'a claim and their Quranic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Murji'a argument that divine punishment is exclusive to disbelievers and the Quranic verses they used as evidence.

Core Idea
The Murji'a restrict God's threat of punishment to non-Muslims alone.

Sanusi now turns to the second of three schools on the execution of the threat: the Murji'a. Unlike the Ash'ari position that punishment for sinful Muslims is possible, the Murji'a hold that God's punishment is reserved exclusively for disbelievers. In this passage, Sanusi presents their claim and the verses they used to support it, though his refutation is not included here.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Notice the rhythm of the Murji'a argument as Sanusi presents it.
The passage is incomplete, ending mid-sentence.
2
Identify each Quranic proof
List the verses the Murji'a cite. For each, consider how they interpret it to support their claim that punishment is only for disbelievers.
The verses are: 16:27, 3:192, 20:48, 67:8, 92:15-16, 34:17.
3
Reflect on the implication
If punishment is only for disbelievers, what happens to Muslims who die unrepentant of major sins? This sets up the Ash'ari refutation.
The Ash'ari view allows for temporary punishment of Muslims by God's will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المذهب الثاني : أنَّ العذابَ إنَّما يحسنُ في حق الكافر دونَ المسلم ، وهو مذهب المرجئة ، وجزموا بنفي عقابِ مَنْ مَاتَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الكبائر قبل أن يُوفَّق للتوبة واحتجوا بقولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ إِنَّ الْخِزْيَ الْيَوْمَ وَالسُّوءَ عَلَى الْكَفِرِينَ [النحل : ۲۷] ، ودخولُ النارِ خزي ؛ بدليل : ﴿ مَن تُدْخِلِ النَّارَ فَقَدْ أَخْزَيْنَتَهُ ﴾ [آل عمران : ۱۹۲] ، فهو خاص إذاً بالكافرين . وبقوله تعالى : قَدْ أُوحِيَ إِلَيْنَا أَنَّ الْعَذَابَ عَلَى مَن كَذَّبَ وَتَوَلَّى [طه : ٤٨] ، والألفُ واللام في ( العذابِ ) : للعموم . وبقولِهِ تعالى : ( كُلَّمَا أُلْقِيَ فِيهَا فوج ...) [الملك : 8) الآية . فَوْجُ وبقوله تعالى : لَا يَصْلَنَهَا إِلَّا الْأَشْقَى * الَّذِي كَذَّبَ وَتَوَلَّى [الليل : ١٥ - ١٦ ] . وبقولِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ : ﴿ وَهَلْ تُجرِى إِلَّا الْكَفُور ) [سبا : ۱۷] ، والكَفُورُ :
The second school: That punishment is only fitting for the disbeliever, not for the Muslim – and this is the school of the Murji'a. They affirm the negation of punishment for whoever dies among the people of major sins before being granted repentance. They argued by His saying: 'Indeed, disgrace and evil today are upon the disbelievers' (Q. 16:27), and entering the fire is disgrace, by the evidence: 'Whoever You admit into the fire, You have disgraced him' (Q. 3:192), so it is specific to the disbelievers. And by His saying: 'It has been revealed to us that the punishment is upon whoever denies and turns away' (Q. 20:48), and the definite article (alif and lam) in 'al-ʿadhāb' (the punishment) indicates generality. And by His saying: 'Every time a group is thrown into it...' (Q. 67:8) the verse. [fragment] And by His saying: 'None shall enter it except the most wretched, who denies and turns away' (Q. 92:15-16). And by His saying, Exalted and Glorified: 'And is anyone recompensed except the ungrateful?' (Q. 34:17), and 'al-kafūr' (the ungrateful) is...
Source pages p. 629

Commentary
This passage presents the second of the three schools on the execution of the threat: the view of the Murji'a. Sanusi explains that the Murji'a hold that punishment in the afterlife is only appropriate for disbelievers, not for Muslims who commit major sins. They affirm categorically that no Muslim who dies without repentance will be punished. They support this with several Quranic verses. First, Q. 16:27 states that disgrace is upon the disbelievers; they argue that entering the Fire is a disgrace, so it must be specific to disbelievers (citing Q. 3:192). Second, Q. 20:48 says punishment is upon those who deny and turn away; they take the definite article in 'al-ʿadhāb' as indicating all punishment is for them. Third, they cite Q. 67:8 about groups being thrown into the Fire (though the text is fragmentary). Fourth, Q. 92:15-16 restricts entry to the most wretched who deny. Fifth, Q. 34:17 asks rhetorically who is recompensed except the ungrateful (al-kafūr). The passage ends abruptly with 'al-kafūr', without presenting Sanusi's refutation. The Murji'a use these verses to argue that punishment is exclusive to non-Muslims, but the Ash'ari position would be that God may punish sinful Muslims at His will, though ultimately they may be saved through intercession or mercy.

Key Terms
المرجئة
نفي عقاب
الكبائر
التوبة
الخزي
العذاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Murji'a position is identical to Sunni orthodoxy.
Correction: Sunni (Ash'ari/Maturidi) theology allows for temporary punishment of sinful Muslims by God's will; the Murji'a absolutely deny any punishment for Muslims.

Checkpoint
Which verse did the Murji'a use to argue that the definite article 'al-' in 'al-ʿadhāb' implies generality?
A) Q. 16:27
B) Q. 20:48
C) Q. 67:8
D) Q. 34:17

Key Takeaway
The Murji'a assert that no Muslim who commits major sins will be punished, using Quranic verses they interpret as restricting punishment to disbelievers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever allowed yourself to think that because you are Muslim, your major sins will not be punished? How does the Murji'a position—though rejected by orthodoxy—subtly influence your own sense of accountability? What would it mean for you to fully accept that every sin matters to God? Write down one sin you have minimized and commit to addressing it this week.
?
The Murji'a use verses that seem to limit punishment to disbelievers. Are there verses in the Quran about punishment for sinful believers that you have ignored or explained away? What would change in your daily life if you truly believed that God's justice applies to you as a Muslim? Name one specific habit you would start or stop.

All Companions are 'Udul: Evidence from Quran and Sunnah
Commentary affirms collective justice of all Sahaba with textual proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all Companions of the Prophet are considered just and trustworthy without investigation, based on Quranic verses and hadiths.

Core Idea
Every Companion is inherently trustworthy; no character check needed.

This lesson presents the foundational Sunni belief that all Companions are 'udul (just). The commentator affirms this position, supported by explicit Quranic praises and prophetic hadiths. We will explore the evidence and its implications for hadith acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the key terms: صحابة, عدالة, عدول.
2
Understand the claim
The claim is that every person whose Companionship is established is accepted without investigating their 'adalah. This is the position of the majority of scholars.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Three verses are cited: 48:29 (praising those with the Prophet), 2:143 (middle nation), 3:110 (best nation). Reflect on how these imply collective virtue.
4
Examine the prophetic hadiths
Three hadiths are cited: 'Companions are like stars', 'Best of centuries is my century', and the hadith about spending gold like Uhud. These show their high status.
5
Reflect on the implication
The consequence is that all narrations from Companions are accepted without scrutiny of their personal character. This principle is foundational in Sunni hadith methodology.
This does not mean all Companions are infallible, but they are reliable in transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولُه : ( والصحابةُ كلُّهم عدول ) هذا هو الذي عليه جمهورُ العلماء والمحققونَ مِنْ أهلِ الأصولِ ؛ أنَّ كلَّ مَنْ ثبَتَتْ صحبتُهُ لا يُسأل عن عدالتِهِ ، ولا يُتوقَّفُ في روايتِهِ ، عُرِفَ أو لم يُعْرَفْ. ودليلهم : ظاهرُ الكتاب والسنَّةِ ؛ كقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَالَّذِينَ مَعَهُ أَشِدَّاءَ عَلَى الْكُفَّارِ رُحَمَاءُ بَيْنَهُمْ ... ﴾ [الفتح : ۲۹] الآيةَ ، وقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَكَذَلِكَ جَعَلْتَكُمْ أُمَّةً وَسَطًا ... ﴾ [البقرة : ١٤٣] الآيةَ ، وقوله : ﴿ كُنتُمْ خَيْرَ أُمَّةٍ أُخْرِجَتْ لِلنَّاسِ ... ﴾ [آل عمران : ۱۱۰] الآيةَ ، وقولِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( أَصْحَابِي كَالنُّجُومِ ؛ بِأَيِّهِمُ اقْتَدَيْتُمُ اهْتَدَيْتُمْ )، وقوله : « خَيْرُ الْقُرُونِ قَرْنِي »، وقولِهِ : « لَوْ أَنْفَقَ أَحَدُكُمْ مِثْلَ أُحُدٍ ذَهَباً ...
His saying: 'And all the Companions are 'udul (just/trustworthy).' This is what the majority of scholars and the verifiers among the people of usul hold: that everyone whose Companionship is established is not asked about his 'adalah (justice), nor is his narration held back from, whether known or unknown. And their evidence is the apparent meaning of the Book and the Sunnah, such as His saying, the Most High: 'And those who are with him are severe against the disbelievers, merciful among themselves...' [al-Fath 48:29] the verse, and His saying, the Most High: 'And thus We have made you a middle nation...' [al-Baqarah 2:143] the verse, and His saying: 'You are the best nation brought forth for mankind...' [Aal 'Imran 3:110] the verse, and his saying, may Allah bless him and grant him peace: 'My Companions are like stars; by whichever of them you follow, you will be guided,' and his saying: 'The best of centuries is my century,' and his saying: 'If one of you were to spend the equivalent of Uhud in gold...'
Source pages p. 636

Commentary
This passage affirms the collective justice (ʿadālah) of all Companions of the Prophet. The commentator reports that this is the position of the majority of scholars and the verifiers among the people of usul al-fiqh. Whoever's Companionship (ṣuḥbah) is established is not investigated concerning his ʿadālah, nor is his narration rejected, whether his character is known or unknown. Then the commentator provides evidence from the Quran and Sunnah: several verses praising the Companions (Qur'an 48:29, 2:143, 3:110), and hadiths such as 'My Companions are like stars; by whichever of them you follow, you will be guided,' 'The best of centuries is my century,' and a hadith about spending gold like Mount Uhud (which implies their precedence and virtue). This establishes the absolute reliability of all Companions in matters of transmission and testimony, a foundational principle in Sunni ʿaqīdah and ḥadīth methodology.

Key Terms
صحابة
عدالة
عدول
رواية
جمهور العلماء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only famous Companions are reliable; those unknown need verification.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that every person whose Companionship is established is accepted without investigation, whether known or unknown.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a Companion whose character is unknown?
A) His narration is rejected
B) He is not asked about his 'adalah and his narration is accepted
C) He must be known to be accepted
D) His 'adalah must be verified by two witnesses

Key Takeaway
All Companions are just and their narrations are accepted without investigation, proven by Quran and Sunnah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear criticisms of certain Companions in historical conflicts, do you find yourself questioning their integrity? How does this lesson's principle that every Companion is 'adl challenge you to trust them all equally, even when your understanding is limited?
?
The Prophet said, 'My Companions are like stars; by whichever you follow, you are guided.' Are there any Companions you instinctively avoid following—maybe because of your school, sect, or personal preference? What would it cost you to submit fully to this hadith and honor all of them?
?
This lesson says a Companion's narration is accepted 'whether known or unknown.' Does your heart accept that? Or is there a subtle arrogance that demands proof of character from those before you? Ask yourself: am I willing to receive truth from any Companion without reservation?

Definition of a Companion and Their Collective Justice
The author defines the Companion and affirms the justice of all Companions without distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni definition of a Companion (Sahabi) and the basis for the collective justice of all Companions.

Core Idea
A Companion is anyone who met the Prophet as a believer and died a believer, regardless of narration length.

This passage from Sanusi's work establishes who qualifies as a Companion of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and why all Companions are considered upright (adl). The author clarifies the correct definition according to the majority of Sunni scholars and defends it against alternative views. He also explains that even a brief meeting with the Prophet bestows immense spiritual benefit, which underpins the collective justice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the translation. Pay attention to the definition and the key phrase 'he who met'.
Notice that the passage begins by dismissing other opinions.
2
Identify the argument for collective justice
The author states that all Companions are upright without distinction. Look for the reason he gives: the immense blessing of any meeting with the Prophet.
This argument relies on the unique status of the Prophet.
3
Consider the analogy with saints
The author draws an analogy with saints who achieve great spiritual progress through a single glance. Reflect on how this supports the claim about Companions.
The analogy highlights the Prophet's unparalleled light.

(1) Neither the measure of one of them nor its half reached. (2) And on this issue there are other unsatisfactory opinions. And if it is observed that many saints, through a single glance or a single attention, achieve great elevation, how much more so when meeting the most noble of creation, whose light is the origin of all lights, and in whose least light all the lights and knowledge of the saints are submerged! Commentary
This passage defines the term 'Companion' (Sahabi) according to the majority of Sunni scholars and affirms the collective justice (adala) of all Companions. It begins by stating that there are unsatisfactory opinions on this issue, but the correct view is that all Companions are upright without distinction. Then it provides the definition: a Companion is one who met the Prophet as a believer and died as a believer, regardless of whether he narrated hadith or the length of companionship. The author prefers the phrase 'he who met' over 'he who saw' because the latter would exclude blind Companions like 'Abdullah ibn Umm Maktum. The explanation then justifies why the length of companionship is not required: even a brief meeting with the Prophet bestows immense spiritual benefits due to his lofty status. The author draws an analogy with saints who achieve great progress through a single glance. This underscores the unique status of the Prophet. The passage concludes with a prayer for the Prophet.

Correction: The author clarifies that even a brief meeting as a believer, with no narration, suffices to be a Companion.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position is that all Companions are upright and every believer who met the Prophet as a believer and died a believer is a Companion, regardless of the length of association.

?

Views on Preferring Companions and the Sunni Consensus
The author presents different views on tafdil and states the Sunni position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different sectarian views on preferring among the Companions and the Sunni consensus on their ranking.

Core Idea
Sunni tradition affirms a clear merit hierarchy among the Companions.

This passage from Sanusi addresses a sensitive issue: how to rank the Companions. Different sects have favoured different figures, but the Sunni position is a consensus on the order of the four caliphs and other virtuous groups. Let's explore the views and the authoritative Sunni ranking.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation to grasp the overall argument: Sanusi first presents the differing views on tafdil, then establishes the Sunni consensus.
Pay attention to the groups mentioned and their preferred Companions.
2
Identify the sectarian views
List the groups: those who abstain from ranking, al-Khattabiyya, al-Rawandiyya, the Shi'a, and Ahl al-Sunna. Note who each group prefers.
Al-Khattabiyya prefer Umar, al-Rawandiyya prefer al-Abbas, Shi'a prefer Ali, Ahl al-Sunna prefer Abu Bakr.
3
Understand the Sunni consensus
Read the quotes from al-Qurtubi and al-Qadi 'Iyad. They affirm that the best is Abu Bakr, then Umar, and that the ranking of all Companions is based on specific groups: the four caliphs, the ten, Badr, Uhud, Bay'at al-Ridwan.
Al-Qadi 'Iyad's quote provides the detailed hierarchy.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this ranking matters in Sunni theology: it reflects the virtue and precedence of the Companions, and it counters the views of sects like the Shi'a who prefer Ali over Abu Bakr.

His saying: 'And the best of them is Abu Bakr, then 'Umar...' etc.: This issue, people differed over it. A group said: one should not engage in preferring among them, and they said: they are like fingers on the palm. Others held the view of preferring, then they differed: al-Khattabiyya preferred 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him; al-Rawandiyya preferred al-'Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him; the Shi'a preferred 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with him; and the Ahl al-Sunna preferred Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him. Al-Qurtubi said in his commentary on Sahih Muslim: 'The predecessors and successors did not differ that the best of them is Abu Bakr, then 'Umar, and no attention is paid to the opinion of the Shi'a and innovators.' Al-Qadi 'Iyad said in al-Ikmal: 'Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi said: Our school are in consensus that the best of them are the four caliphs in the order of their caliphate, then the remaining ten, then the people of Badr, then the people of Uhud, then the people of Bay'at al-Ridwan, and whoever has a special merit: the people of the two pledges from...' (1) See Ikmal al-Mu'lim (7/379) and al-Mufhim (6/248, 252).
Source pages p. 638

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of tafdil (preferring among the Companions). It first reports that some groups abstain from any ranking, likening the Companions to fingers on the palm. Others engage in preferring but differ: al-Khattabiyya prefer 'Umar, al-Rawandiyya prefer al-'Abbas, the Shi'a prefer 'Ali, and Ahl al-Sunna prefer Abu Bakr. Then it quotes al-Qurtubi confirming the consensus of early and later scholars that Abu Bakr is best, followed by 'Umar, dismissing the views of Shi'a and innovators. Finally, al-Qadi 'Iyad quotes Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi on the detailed ranking: first the four rightly-guided caliphs in order, then the remaining ten promised paradise, then the participants of Badr, then Uhud, then the Pledge of Ridwan, and those with special virtue like the two pledges.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that ranking Companions is entirely discouraged and that they are all equal in virtue.
Correction: While some groups abstain from ranking, the Sunni tradition explicitly affirms a hierarchy based on merit, with Abu Bakr as the best, followed by Umar, and so on.

D) The remaining ten, then Bay'at al-Ridwan, then the people of Badr, then the people of Uhud

Key Takeaway
The Sunni consensus ranks the Companions: Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali, then the remaining ten, then the people of Badr, then the people of Uhud, then the people of Bay'at al-Ridwan.

?

Disagreement on the Merits of Uthman and Ali
Presents differing views on ranking Uthman and Ali and the positions of Ash'ari and Malik.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main scholarly views on the relative merits of Uthman and Ali, and the positions of al-Ash'ari and Imam Malik on this issue.

Core Idea
Scholars differ on whether to rank Uthman and Ali by caliphal order or suspend judgment.

This lesson addresses a theological and historical discussion among Ahl al-Sunna regarding the ranking of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, specifically between Uthman and Ali. The author presents the two main positions—one that follows the order of their caliphate, held by al-Ash'ari, and another that suspends judgment, favored by Imam Malik. Through a reported exchange, we see Malik's reluctance to declare superiority between them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own words and flow of opinions come through.
Notice the use of 'قيل' to introduce differing views.
2
Identify the two main views
The passage presents two opinions on ranking Uthman and Ali. Find them and note which scholar is associated with each.
The view of al-Ash'ari and the view of Imam Malik are contrasted.
3
Examine Malik's response in the Mudawwana
Read the anecdote where Malik is asked about the best after the Prophet. Notice his clear ranking of Abu Bakr and Umar, but his refusal to rank Uthman and Ali.
Malik says he hasn't found anyone he follows who preferred one over the other.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this disagreement matters in Sunni theology. It shows a range of permissible opinions and a principle of caution in weighing the merits of Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختُلِفَ فيما بينَ عثمان وعلي رضي الله تعالى عنهما : فقيل : هما على ترتيبهما في الخلافة ، وإليه مالَ الأشعري . وقيل فيهما بالوقفِ ، وإليه نحا مالكٌ رحمه الله تعالى ، فقيل لهُ في ( المدونة » : مَنْ أفضلُ الناس بعد نبيهم ؟ فقال : أبو بكرٍ ثم عمرُ ، أوَفي ذلكَ شكٌ ؟! وسقطَ ( عمرُ ) مِنْ بعض الرواياتِ ، قيل : فعلي وعثمانُ ؟ فقال : ما أدركتُ أحداً ممَّنْ أقتدي بهِ يُفضّلُ أحدهما على الآخر ، ولأبي المعالي قريب منه
And there was disagreement concerning Uthman and Ali, may God be pleased with them both: it was said: they are according to their order in the caliphate, and al-Ash'ari inclined to that. And it was said regarding them: suspension (al-waqf), and Malik, may God have mercy on him, inclined to that. So it was said to him in al-Mudawwana: 'Who is the most excellent of people after their Prophet?' He said: 'Abu Bakr, then Umar. Or is there doubt about that?' And (Umar) fell from some narrations. It was said: 'What about Ali and Uthman?' He said: 'I have not found anyone whom I follow who prefers one of them over the other.' And Abu al-Ma'ali has a similar opinion.
Source pages p. 639

Commentary
This passage presents the disagreement among scholars on the relative merits of Uthman and Ali, may God be pleased with them. The author states that two main views exist: one that they are ranked according to their order in the caliphate (i.e., Uthman then Ali, since Uthman was the third caliph and Ali the fourth), and this view was adopted by al-Ash'ari. The second view is suspension (al-waqf), meaning withholding judgment on which is superior, and this was the inclination of Imam Malik. The author then reports a famous incident from al-Mudawwana where Malik was asked: 'Who is the most excellent of people after their Prophet?' He answered: 'Abu Bakr, then Umar. Or is there doubt about that?' When asked about Ali and Uthman, he replied: 'I have not found anyone whom I follow who prefers one of them over the other.' This indicates that Malik suspended judgment on the relative ranking of Uthman and Ali. The author notes that Abu al-Ma'ali (Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni) has a similar stance.

Key Terms
الوقف
التفضيل
الخلافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that suspending judgment means equating Uthman and Ali in merit.
Correction: Suspending judgment (waqf) means refraining from declaring which is superior, not necessarily asserting they are equal. It is a position of scholarly caution.

Checkpoint
What was the view of al-Ash'ari regarding the ranking of Uthman and Ali?
A) He suspended judgment.
B) He held that they are ranked according to their order in the caliphate.
C) He preferred Ali over Uthman.
D) He preferred Uthman over Ali.

Key Takeaway
The disagreement on the merits of Uthman and Ali reflects a broader principle of caution in ranking Companions, with some prioritizing historical order and others preferring restraint.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about the Companions, do you find yourself ranking them in your heart? What does this lesson teach you about the danger of trying to decide who is better when the early scholars themselves refrained? Will you adopt a posture of humility and refrain from speaking about their ranks beyond what is established?
?
Are you comfortable living with uncertainty about the merits of the Companions, or do you feel the need to settle every matter of preference? How can the example of Imam Malik's restraint guide you in matters where you have no definitive knowledge?
?
Do you sometimes harbor opinions about people based on limited information, even about the Companions? How can you guard your tongue from speaking about their relative merits without clear evidence?

Ibn al-Arabi's Critique of Preferring Umar over Abu Bakr
Ibn al-Arabi criticizes al-Fihri and affirms Abu Bakr's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn al-Arabi's argument that Abu Bakr's superiority is undisputed among Ahl al-Sunnah, and why preferring Umar over him is a clear error.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr is the undisputed master of the community.

This passage presents a sharp critique from Ibn al-Arabi against his own teacher, al-Fihri, who used to prefer Umar over Abu Bakr. Ibn al-Arabi firmly corrects this view, asserting that proper consideration reveals Abu Bakr's unmatched rank. The lesson examines the evidence and the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah on this matter.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Note the direct critique of al-Fihri and the strong statement about Abu Bakr.
2
Understand the critique
Identify why Ibn al-Arabi says al-Fihri 'did not hit the mark of correct consideration.' Consider what 'correct consideration' would entail.
Ibn al-Arabi implies that if al-Fihri had reflected properly, he would have known Abu Bakr's superiority.
3
Reflect on the consensus
Recognize that this passage affirms the Sunni consensus that Abu Bakr is the sayyid (master) of the Ummah, a position that is undisputed (ghayr mudafa').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالَ ابنُ العربي : قد كانَ شيخُنا الفهري يُقدِّمُ عمر كثيراً ، ويقول : لو قال أحدٌ بتقديمه على أبي بكرٍ لقلتُه ، ويرحم الله الفهري ، لم يصب وجْهَ النظرِ ، بل غابَ عنهُ ؛ إذْ لو نظر لعلم أنَّ أبا بكرٍ رضيَ الله تعالى عنه سيِّدُ الأمَّةِ غيرَ مُدافَعِ
And Ibn al-Arabi said: 'Our teacher al-Fihri used to greatly prefer Umar, and he would say: If someone said to give him precedence over Abu Bakr, I would say it. May God have mercy on al-Fihri, he did not hit the mark of correct consideration, rather he was oblivious to it; for if he had considered, he would have known that Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him, is the master of the community, undeniable.'
Source pages p. 639

Commentary
This passage is a critique by Ibn al-Arabi of his teacher al-Fihri. Ibn al-Arabi reports that al-Fihri used to greatly prefer Umar over others and even claimed that if someone said that Umar should be given precedence over Abu Bakr, he would say so. Ibn al-Arabi then criticizes this view, saying that al-Fihri did not consider the matter correctly and was oblivious to the truth. If he had reflected, he would have known that Abu Bakr is the master (sayyid) of the Muslim community, a fact that is undeniable (ghayr mudafa'). This passage emphasizes the consensus among Ahl al-Sunnah on the superiority of Abu Bakr.

Key Terms
سيِّد الأمَّة
غير مُدافَع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Preferring Umar over Abu Bakr is a valid difference of opinion among scholars.
Correction: Ibn al-Arabi asserts that this is a clear error; Abu Bakr's superiority is undeniable and agreed upon by Ahl al-Sunnah.

Checkpoint
What did Ibn al-Arabi say about al-Fihri's view on Umar's precedence?
A) He agreed with it.
B) He criticized it, stating Abu Bakr is the master of the community.
C) He said al-Fihri was correct in preferring Umar.
D) He remained silent.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's superiority over all other companions is an undisputed Sunni doctrine, as affirmed by Ibn al-Arabi.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were in a discussion with someone who preferred another companion over Abu Bakr, how would you respond based on the precise argument in this passage? Are you willing to correct even a respected teacher if they err? What holds you back?
?
Ibn al-Arabi did not spare his own teacher from criticism. Is there a person in your life—a teacher, scholar, or relative—whose view on a matter of creed you know to be wrong but have not addressed? What would it cost you to speak the truth as he did?
?
The phrase 'غير مُدافَع' (undeniable) is used for Abu Bakr's status. Are there any matters of creed that you treat as 'mudafa' (debatable) that should be 'ghayr mudafa'? How does this challenge your current approach to learning 'aqeedah?
