Interpretations of Malik's Waqf and the Meaning of Tafdil
Discusses interpretations of Malik's waqf and defines tafdil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different interpretations of Imam Malik's suspension of judgment regarding Uthman and Ali, and the correct definition of tafdil (preference) as abundance of reward and rank.

Core Idea
Imam Malik's silence was not neutrality but a cautious stance amid sectarian strife.

In this passage, the author discusses the various explanations given for Imam Malik's reported suspension of judgment on the relative merits of Uthman and Ali. Some took it literally, others saw it as a reference to the caliphal order, and yet others attributed it to the political pressures of his time. The passage then clarifies that tafdil (preference) specifically refers to greater reward and higher rank in the afterlife, not worldly evaluation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the author's structure come through.
The passage has two parts: interpretations of waqf and definition of tafdil.
2
Identify the three interpretations of Malik's waqf
Notice the sequence: 'قيل' introduces each interpretation. The first is literal suspension, the second refers back to the first view (order of caliphate), and the third is due to political partisanship.
3
Understand the meaning of tafdil
Focus on the sentence 'معنى التفضيل: كثرة الثواب ورفع الدرجة'. Tafdil is not about worldly merit but divine reward and rank.
The sentence is incomplete in the source, but the key definition is given.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this clarification matters: it prevents partisanship and reminds us that ultimate preference is known only through revelation.
This guards against using personal opinion to judge the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اختلف في تأويل وقفِ مالك رحمهُ اللهُ تعالى ؛ فقيل : هو وقفٌ على ظاهره ، وقيل : هو راجع للقولِ الأَوَّلِ ؛ أنَّهم على ترتيبهم في الخلافة ، ويحتمل وقفُهُ وقفُ مَنْ يُقتدَى بِهِ أنَّهُ لما وقعَ مِنَ الاختلافِ والتعصب ، حتى صارَ الناسُ فرقتين ؛ علويَّةً وعثمانيَّةً ، وقد قيل : إِنَّ بسبب قوله بالتفضيل بينهما طلبَتْهُ العَلَوِيَّةُ حتى امتحِنَ رَحمَهُ الله تعالى . ومعنى التفضيل : كثرةُ الثوابِ ورفع الدرجةِ ، وذلكَ لا يُدرَكُ
Then they differed regarding the interpretation of the suspension (waqf) of Malik, may God have mercy on him. It was said: it is suspension in its literal sense. And it was said: it refers back to the first view, that they are according to their order in the caliphate. And it is possible that his suspension and the suspension of those who follow him was due to the occurrence of disagreement and partisanship, until people became two factions: Alawiyya and Uthmaniyya. And it was said: because of his saying that preference between them, the Alawiyya sought him until he was tested, may God have mercy on him. And the meaning of preference (al-tafdil) is abundance of reward and elevation of rank, and that is not known...
Source pages p. 640

Commentary
This passage deals with the interpretation of Imam Malik's reported stance of suspension (waqf) regarding Uthman and Ali. Three interpretations are given. First, that Malik meant literal suspension, i.e., not declaring a preference. Second, that his suspension actually refers back to the first view (ranking by order of caliphate), meaning he did have a view but refrained from stating it openly. Third, that his suspension and that of those who follow him was due to the political circumstances of his time, when people had split into Alawiyya (supporters of Ali) and Uthmaniyya (supporters of Uthman) factions, and there was partisanship. Some even said that because of his statement about preferring one over the other (or his statement of suspension), the Alawiyya faction sought him out and he was tested (imtihan). The author then defines what 'preference' (tafdil) means in this context: it is abundance of reward and elevation of rank. The sentence ends incomplete, but the point is that preference is not known through reason but through revelation. This guards against the view that preference can be determined by personal opinion.

Key Terms
الوقف
التفضيل
العلويَّة
العثمانيَّة
الثواب
الدرجة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Imam Malik's suspension means he had no opinion on the superiority of Uthman and Ali.
Correction: The passage shows that Malik's suspension was likely a cautious response due to political tensions, not an absence of opinion. The third interpretation explicitly ties it to partisanship.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT an interpretation given for Imam Malik's suspension?
A) It was literal suspension.
B) It referred back to the view of ranking by caliphate order.
C) It was due to the political partisanship of the time.
D) It was because Malik considered them equal in merit.

Key Takeaway
Imam Malik's suspension of judgment on Uthman and Ali was a prudent response to sectarian strife, and tafdil means greater reward and rank, not worldly preference.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When faced with a conflict between two respected figures, do you have the courage to remain silent like Malik, or do you rush to judge? How does this lesson challenge your impulse to take sides?
?
The lesson says tafdil is about reward and rank in the afterlife, not worldly preference. How does your own assessment of people's status in this world conflict with this divine standard? Will you let this lesson recalibrate your judgments?
?
The Alawiyya sought out Malik because of his statement on preference. Have you ever been persecuted for a truth you held? Or have you hidden your beliefs to avoid conflict? What does Malik's courage teach you about standing firm in truth despite consequences?

Interpreting Malik's Suspension on Uthman and Ali
Enumeration of three interpretations of Malik's waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three interpretations of Imam Malik's suspension of judgment regarding the relative merit of Uthman and Ali.

Core Idea
Malik's 'waqf' may reflect caution, not uncertainty.

Imam Malik famously withheld judgment on who was superior between Uthman and Ali after Abu Bakr and Umar. Scholars differed on why he did so. This passage presents the main interpretations and hints at a possible reason related to sectarian strife.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Malik's waqf
Read the Arabic passage about the differing interpretations of Malik's suspension. Then read the translation to grasp the three views.
Notice the three interpretations: apparent meaning, referring back to the first opinion, and due to sectarianism.
2
Identify the three interpretations
List the three interpretations mentioned: (1) literal suspension, (2) reverting to the first opinion (order of caliphate), (3) suspension due to disagreement and partisanship.
The third interpretation suggests Malik's waqf was a precaution, not indecision.
3
Consider the sectarian context
The passage mentions that people split into Alawiyya and Uthmaniyya parties. Reflect on how this context might have influenced Malik's stance.
The Alawiyya even sought to test Malik because of his statement of preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اختلف في تأويل وقفِ مالك رحمهُ اللهُ تعالى ؛ فقيل : هو وقفٌ على ظاهره ، وقيل : هو راجع للقولِ الأَوَّلِ؛ أنَّهم على ترتيبهم في الخلافة ، ويحتمل وقفُهُ وقفُ مَنْ يُقتدَى بِهِ أنَّهُ لما وقعَ مِنَ الاختلافِ والتعصب (۱)، حتى صارَ الناسُ فرقتين؛ علويَّةً وعثمانيَّةً، وقد قيل : إِنَّ بسبب قوله بالتفضيل بينهما طلبَتْهُ العَلَوِيَّةُ حتى امتحِنَ رَحمَهُ الله تعالى (۲) ومعنى التفضيل : كثرةُ الثوابِ ورفع الدرجةِ، وذلكَ لا يُدرَكُ بقياس، وإنَّما يثبتُ بالنقل، ولا يُستدَلُّ عليه بكثرة الطاعاتِ الظاهرة؛ إذْ قد يكونُ (۱) على اليسيرِ مِنْ عملِ السِّرِّ أكثرَ مِنَ الكثيرِ الظاهر، وإنْ كانَتِ الأعمال الظاهرة فيها مجال لغلبة الظن بالتفضيل
Then they differed regarding the interpretation of Malik's suspension (waqf) - may Allah have mercy on him: it was said: it is a suspension according to its apparent meaning, and it was said: it refers back to the first statement, that they are in the order of the caliphate. And it is possible that his suspension (waqf) and the suspension of one who is followed (yaqtada bihi) is because of what occurred of disagreement and partisanship (1), until people became two parties: Alawiyya and Uthmaniyya. And it was said: that because of his statement of preference between them, the Alawiyya sought him until he was tested - may Allah have mercy on him (2). And the meaning of tafdil (preference) is abundance of reward and elevation of rank. And that is not known by analogy, but rather it is established by transmission (naql). And it is not inferred by the abundance of outward acts of obedience, for it may be that (1) the reward in a small secret deed is greater than the plentiful outward one, even though outward deeds have room for preponderance of conjecture (ghalabat al-zann) regarding preference.
Source pages p. 640

Commentary
This passage discusses different interpretations of Malik's suspension of judgment (waqf) concerning the relative merit of Uthman and Ali after Abu Bakr and Umar. Some take it literally, meaning Malik did not prefer one over the other. Others say he reverted to the first opinion that they follow the order of the caliphate. A third possibility is that his suspension was due to sectarian strife, not uncertainty. The passage then defines tafdil as greater reward and rank, emphasizing that it is known only through transmitted reports, not rational analogy or outward deeds. Outward deeds may give strong conjecture but not certainty.

تأويل
علوية
عثمانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Malik's waqf means he was uncertain or had no opinion on the matter.
Correction: The third interpretation shows his waqf may have been a precaution due to sectarianism, not indecision.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one possible reason for Malik's suspension?
A) He had no knowledge on the matter
B) Sectarian disagreement and partisanship
C) He preferred Uthman over Ali
D) He was forced by the ruler

Key Takeaway
Imam Malik's suspension of judgment on the relative merit of Uthman and Ali can be interpreted in multiple ways, including as a precaution against sectarian strife.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The Alawiyya tested Malik because he expressed a preference. Have you ever been tested by others for your beliefs? How did you respond, and what does that response say about your reliance on truth versus social approval?

Meaning of Tafdil and Its Basis
Definition and epistemological basis of tafdil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of tafdil (preference) and why it can only be known through transmitted reports, not reason or outward deeds.

Core Idea
Preference in reward is known by revelation, not analogy.

After discussing Malik's suspension, the author defines tafdil and clarifies its epistemological basis. He emphasizes that true superiority in reward and rank is not accessible through rational analogy or even abundant outward worship, but only through divine revelation. This principle is crucial for understanding debates about the relative merits of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on tafdil
Read the Arabic passage defining tafdil and its basis. Then read the translation carefully.
Notice the three key points: definition of tafdil, its source (naql), and the limitation of outward deeds.
2
Understand the definition of tafdil
Tafdil is defined as abundance of reward and elevation of rank. This is a qualitative, not quantitative, measure.
3
Identify the sources of knowledge
The passage states that tafdil cannot be known through analogy (qiyas) but only through transmission (naql). Also, outward deeds alone are not sufficient, as a small hidden deed may be more rewardable.
This counters rationalist approaches to ranking Companions.
4
Reflect on the role of conjecture
The passage concedes that outward deeds give room for strong conjecture (ghalabat al-zann), but not certainty about preference.
So outward deeds can inform opinion, but not establish definitive preference.

Disagreement on Whether Tafdil is Definitive or Probable
Sanusi records two views on the certainty of tafdil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate among scholars who affirm tafdil over whether its ruling is definitive (qat'i) or probable (zanni), and the evidence cited for each position.

Core Idea
Even among those who affirm tafdil, there is disagreement: is it certain or merely probable?

This lesson examines a further disagreement within the camp that affirms the preferability of the best of mankind. While all these scholars hold that tafdil is true, they differ on its epistemological certainty. Al-Ash'ari considered it definitive, citing a strong statement from Imam Malik, while the Qadi considered it a matter of ijtihad, hence probable. This passage from Sanusi presents both views concisely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two positions
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it begins by stating that those who affirm tafdil disagreed, then presents two views: one definitive, one probable.
The passage is short but dense. Pay attention to the evidence cited for each view.
2
Examine the evidence for the definitive view
The definitive view is supported by Malik's rhetorical question in al-Mudawwana: 'Is there any doubt about that?!' This indicates strong certainty.
Al-Ash'ari inclined toward this position.
3
Examine the evidence for the probable view
The Qadi argues it is probable because the issue is a matter of ijtihad; one who leaves off considering it does not sin. This shows the issue is not definitively settled.
Consider the implications of each epistemological stance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف القائلون بالتفضيل : فقيل : هو قطعي، ومالَ إليه الأشعري، وإليه يشير قول مالك في المدوَّنة في تفضيل أبي بكرٍ: ( أوَفي ذلك شكٌ ؟! (۲) وقال القاضي : ( هو ظني )، قال : ( لأنَّ المسألةَ اجتهاديَّةٌ، لو ترك أحد النظر فيها لم يأثم (۳)
And those who affirmed tafdil differed: it was said: it is definitive (qat'i), and al-Ash'ari inclined towards it, and to that points the statement of Malik in al-Mudawwana regarding the preference of Abu Bakr: 'Is there any doubt about that?!' (2). And the Qadi said: it is probable (zanni), he said: because the issue is a matter of ijtihad; if someone left off considering it, he would not sin (3).
Source pages p. 641

Commentary
Here the author records a further disagreement among those who affirm tafdil: whether it is a certain (qat'i) or probable (zanni) matter. Al-Ash'ari inclined towards certainty, citing Malik's strong rhetorical question about Abu Bakr. The Qadi (likely al-Baqillani or another judge) considered it a matter of ijtihad, meaning it is probable and not sinful to leave it unexamined.

Key Terms
قطعي
ظني
اجتهادي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the disagreement on tafdil is contradictory, but it reflects different epistemological approaches (certainty vs. probability).
Correction: The disagreement is not about whether tafdil is true, but about the degree of certainty with which it is known.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for al-Ash'ari's view that tafdil is definitive?
A) A hadith from the Prophet
B) Malik's statement in al-Mudawwana
C) Consensus of the scholars
D) Rational proof

Key Takeaway
Among scholars who affirm tafdil, there is a difference of opinion on whether it is a certain (qat'i) or probable (zanni) matter, with each view based on different sources of evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself demanding absolute certainty from a scholar's opinion, are you trusting your own desire for control more than Allah's allowance for difference? How will you surrender this need today?
?
Think of a time you dismissed someone else's view on a religious matter because you thought it was 'just their opinion.' In light of the Qadi's argument that not thinking about a matter of ijtihad is not sinful, can you accept that some issues are not for you to judge? What would it cost you to let go of that judgment?
?
Do you secretly believe that having a position on every controversial issue makes you a better Muslim? What does this lesson reveal about humility in the face of scholarly disagreement?

Outward vs Inward Tafdil
Dispute on scope of tafdil: outward and inward or only outward.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different scholarly positions on whether tafdil applies to outward and inward aspects of faith, and the reasoning behind limiting tafdil to outward.

Core Idea
Tafdil is judged by outward appearance because inward reality is hidden.

This passage addresses a subtle but important question in the study of tafdil: does 'superiority' apply to both outward and inward dimensions of a person's faith, or only to what is outwardly apparent? The author presents a dispute and the reasoning of a key scholar (the Qadi) who ultimately favors restricting tafdil to the outward. This discussion helps us understand how theologians balance divine knowledge of the unseen with human assessment based on observable evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Note the two positions mentioned.
The passage includes a footnote marker (4) which is editorial.
2
Identify the two views
The passage states a disagreement: does tafdil apply to both outward and inward, or only outward? Identify each view clearly.
3
Understand the Qadi's reasoning
The Qadi supported both views but relied on the outward-only view. His reason is that the inward may be contrary to what we perceive outwardly. Reflect on why this reasoning is significant.
This highlights that inner states are hidden and cannot be definitively judged by humans.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا اختُلِفَ : هل التفضيلُ في الظاهر والباطن، أو في الظاهر خاصة؟ والقاضي نصرَ كلاً مِنَ القولين واحتج له، وتعويلُهُ على أَنَّهُ في الظاهر فقط؛ قالَ : ( لأنَّه قد يكونُ في الباطن على خلافِ ما عندنا (۴)
And likewise they differed: is tafdil in outward and inward, or only in outward? And the Qadi supported each of the two statements and argued for them, but his reliance is that it is only outward; he said: because it may be that the inward is contrary to what we have (4).
Source pages p. 641

Commentary
This passage addresses whether tafdil applies to both outward (zahir) and inward (batin) aspects or only outward. The Qadi (al-Baqillani or similar) supported both views but ultimately favored outward only, because inner states are unknowable and may differ from outward appearances.

Key Terms
ظاهر
باطن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think tafdil must apply to both outward and inward equally.
Correction: The passage shows a valid scholarly view that tafdil is limited to outward because inner states are hidden and may differ from outward appearances.

Checkpoint
What reason does the Qadi give for restricting tafdil to outward only?
A) Inward is not important
B) Inward may be contrary to what we know
C) There is no evidence for inward
D) Outward is easier to judge

Key Takeaway
The Qadi reasoned that tafdil is outward only because inner states may differ from outward perception, limiting human judgment to the apparent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you catch yourself looking down on someone for their outward sins, what would it mean for you to truly believe that their inner faith might be greater than yours? Can you name one concrete change in your attitude this demands?
?
If you knew that on the Day of Judgment, your outward piety will not shield you if your inward is corrupt, what secret intention or habit would you feel most urgent to repent of right now?
?
The Qadi argues that tafdil is only outward because we cannot know the inner state. Does this make you more humble in your judgments of others, or more fearful of Allah's knowledge of your own hidden faults? What specific step will you take today to act on that awareness?

Preference of Those Who Died During the Prophet's Lifetime
Reports a view on superiority of those who died during the Prophet's lifetime

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the basis for the view that Companions who died during the Prophet's lifetime are superior to those who survived him.

Core Idea
Dying in the Prophet's lifetime indicates special merit.

This lesson presents a specific opinion among scholars regarding the ranking of the Companions. Some held that those who passed away while the Prophet was alive are superior, citing a hadith where the Prophet declares himself a witness for them and his commendation. Let's explore the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the strong opinion expressed: a group held a clear view on superiority.
The passage begins with 'وذهبت طائفة'.
2
Identify the opinion and its proponent
The view is that those who died during the Prophet's life are better than those who remained. It was chosen by Ibn 'Abd al-Barr.
Ibn 'Abd al-Barr is a famous Maliki scholar.
3
Understand the evidence
The evidence is a hadith: 'I am a witness over these' and the Prophet's commendation and prayer for them. Consider how these show special status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذهبَتْ طائفةٌ: إلى أنَّ مَنْ ماتَ في حياتِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أفضلُ ممَّنْ بقيَ بعدَهُ، واختارَهُ ابنُ عبدِ البرِّ؛ لحديثِ: « أَنَا شَهِيدٌ عَلَى هَؤُلَاءِ (۵)، وتزكية بعضهم وصلاتِهِ عليهم، واختُلِفَ فيما بينَ عائشة وفاطمة رضي الله تعالى عنهما، واحتج كل بأحاديثَ، وتوقف
And a group held: that whoever died during his lifetime - may Allah bless him and grant him peace - is better than those who remained after him, and Ibn 'Abd al-Barr chose it, due to the hadith: 'I am a witness over these' (5), and the commendation of some of them and his prayer over them. And there was disagreement regarding 'A'isha and Fatima - may Allah be pleased with both of them - and each argued with hadiths, and he refrained.
Source pages p. 641

Commentary
This passage reports the opinion that Companions who died during the Prophet's lifetime are superior to those who survived him, citing a hadith where the Prophet says 'I am a witness over these' and his commendation and prayer for them. This view was adopted by Ibn 'Abd al-Barr. It then notes an unresolved dispute between the merits of Aisha and Fatima, each side using hadith evidence, and the author refrains from deciding.

Key Terms
حديث
تزكية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which scholar chose the view that those who died during the Prophet's lifetime are superior?
A) Ibn 'Abd al-Barr
B) Imam Malik
C) Imam Shafi'i
D) Imam Ahmad

Key Takeaway
Some scholars held that Companions who died during the Prophet's lifetime are superior, based on a hadith and the Prophet's commendation.

The Dispute Between Aisha and Fatima
Reports a disagreement over Aisha and Fatima and the author's stance of refraining

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that there is a known disagreement over the relative merits of Aisha and Fatima, and that the author refrains from giving a preference.

Core Idea
The merits of Aisha and Fatima are debated; a learned stance is to refrain.

The final part of this passage addresses a famous dispute among the ummah: who is better, Aisha or Fatima? Each side has its proofs. The author, however, chooses not to take a side, demonstrating a scholarly practice of tawaqquf.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the language: 'اختُلِفَ' indicates a disagreement.
The passage ends with 'وتوقف'.
2
Identify the two figures and the nature of the disagreement
The disagreement is between Aisha and Fatima, may Allah be pleased with both. It concerns their relative merit.
Both are revered figures in Islam.
3
Observe the author's position
The author says 'وتوقف', meaning he refrained from choosing a side. This is a scholarly stance of suspending judgment.
Tawaqquf is a valid position in cases of conflicting evidence.

Source Text

And there was disagreement regarding 'A'isha and Fatima - may Allah be pleased with both of them - and each argued with hadiths, and he refrained.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you hear a dispute among righteous people, is your first impulse to judge or to refrain? What does the author's example of using hadith evidence teach you about the need for knowledge before taking a stance?
?
The author simply reports and refrains—no need to prove one is better. Do you feel the need to always determine who is right? Can you accept ambiguity in matters that are not central to your faith? Write one practical commitment to practice tawaqquf this week.

How is Tafḍīl Established? Definitive or Probable?
Sanusi explains the method of establishing tafḍīl and presents the disagreement on its certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the method of establishing tafḍīl among the Companions and the disagreement on whether it is definitive or probable.

Core Idea
Tafḍīl is based on transmission, not analogy, and its certainty is debated.

The issue of preferring some Companions over others is a delicate matter. Scholars first clarified how such preference should be established. Is it by analogy or by transmitted texts? And once established, is the ranking definitive or open to ijtihad? This passage presents the foundational positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on method and certainty
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the two main parts: the method of establishing tafḍīl and the disagreement on its certainty.
The passage uses a very concise style; pay attention to the key terms.
2
Identify the method: not by qiyas
Sanusi explicitly states that tafḍīl is not established by analogy but by transmission, and not by apparent acts of obedience.
3
Contrast the two views on certainty
Note the two opinions: definitive (al-Ash'ari and Malik) and probable (al-Qadi). Understand the reasoning behind each, especially al-Qadi's ijtihad argument.
Al-Qadi's statement is the key to understanding the probable view.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this disagreement affects the way we view rankings among Companions. Is it a matter of certainty or opinion?
This connects to broader discussions in kalam about definitive vs. probable knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بقياس ، وإنَّما يثبتُ بالنقل، ولا يُستدَلُّ عليه بكثرة الطاعاتِ الظاهرة ؛ إذْ قد يكونُ على اليسيرِ مِنْ عملِ السِّرِّ أكثرَ مِنَ الكثيرِ الظاهر ، وإنْ كانَتِ الأعمال الظاهرة فيها مجال لغلبة الظن بالتفضيل واختلف القائلون بالتفضيل : فقيل : هو قطعي ، ومالَ إليه الأشعري ، وإليه يشير قول مالك في المدوَّنة في تفضيل أبي بكرٍ : ( أوَفي ذلك شكٌ ؟! ) وقال القاضي : ( هو ظني ) ، قال : ( لأنَّ المسألةَ اجتهاديَّةٌ ، لو ترك أحد النظر فيها لم يأثم ) وكذا اختُلِفَ : هل التفضيلُ في الظاهر والباطن ، أو في الظاهر خاصة ؟ والقاضي نصرَ كلاً مِنَ القولين واحتج له ، وتعويلُهُ على أَنَّهُ في الظاهر فقط ؛ قالَ : ( لأنَّه قد يكونُ في الباطن على خلافِ ما عندنا ) وذهبَتْ طائفةٌ : إلى أنَّ مَنْ ماتَ في حياتِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أفضلُ ممَّنْ بقيَ بعدَهُ ، واختارَهُ ابنُ عبدِ البرِّ ؛ لحديثِ : « أَنَا شَهِيدٌ عَلَى هَؤُلَاءِ ، وتزكية بعضهم وصلاتِهِ عليهم ، واختُلِفَ فيما بينَ عائشة وفاطمة رضي الله تعالى عنهما ، واحتج كل بأحاديثَ ، وتوقف الأشعري في المسألة وتردَّدَ فيها وبالجملة : فكلُّهم سادات أجلَّةٌ مختارونَ عندَ اللهِ عزَّ وجلَّ ، نفعنا الله تعالى بجميعهم ، وحشرنا في زمرتهم ، وأماتنا على محبَّتِهم والاقتداء بهديهم
By analogy? Rather it is established by transmission, and one does not argue for it by abundance of apparent acts of obedience; for reward may be greater for a small secret deed than for many apparent deeds, even if apparent deeds provide room for the preponderance of opinion regarding preference. And those who hold the view of preference differed: It was said: It is definitive, and al-Ash'ari inclined to this, and the statement of Malik in al-Mudawwana regarding preferring Abu Bakr points to this: 'Is there any doubt about that?' And al-Qadi said: 'It is probable,' he said: 'Because the issue is based on ijtihad; if someone were to leave off consideration of it, he would not sin.' Similarly, it was differed: Is preference in the outward and inward, or only in the outward? Al-Qadi supported both opinions and argued for them, but his reliance is that it is only in the outward; he said: 'Because it may be that in the inward it is contrary to what we have.' And a group held that whoever died during his lifetime—may Allah bless him and grant him peace—is better than those who remained after him, and Ibn 'Abd al-Barr chose this, due to the hadith: 'I am a witness over these,' and the commendation of some of them and his prayer upon them. And it was differed concerning 'A'isha and Fatima—may Allah be pleased with them both—and each argued with hadiths, and al-Ash'ari hesitated and vacillated on the issue. In summary: All of them are noble masters, chosen ones in the sight of Allah Almighty. May Allah benefit us with all of them, gather us in their group, and cause us to die upon love of them and following their guidance.
Source pages p. 641

Commentary
This passage discusses the issue of tafḍīl (preference) among the Companions. It begins by stating that tafḍīl is not determined by qiyas (analogical reasoning) but by transmitted evidence, and not by apparent acts of worship because secret deeds may be more rewarding. Then it presents the disagreement on whether the preference is qaṭ'ī (definitive) or ẓannī (probable), citing al-Ash'ari and Malik for definitive, and al-Qadi for probable. Then it addresses whether preference applies to both outward (ẓāhir) and inward (bāṭin) or only outward, with al-Qadi supporting both but leaning to only outward. Then it mentions a group who prefer those who died in the Prophet's lifetime over those who survived him, citing a hadith. Then it mentions disagreement between 'A'isha and Fatima, with al-Ash'ari hesitating. Finally, it concludes that all Companions are noble and favored, asking for benefit and gathering with them.

Key Terms
تفضيل
قطعي
ظني
اجتهادي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think tafḍīl is definitively known and cannot be subject to ijtihad.
Correction: The passage shows that a respected scholar like al-Qadi held it to be probable based on ijtihad.

Checkpoint
According to al-Qadi, why is the issue of tafḍīl probable (ẓannī) rather than definitive?
A) Because the Companions themselves disagreed.
B) Because it is based on ijtihad and one is not sinful for leaving it.
C) Because there is no textual evidence.
D) Because al-Ash'ari said so.

Key Takeaway
The method of tafḍīl is based on transmission, and its certainty is disputed; al-Qadi held it as probable due to its ijtihad nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hold a belief that you consider certain, have you ever genuinely considered that a respected scholar might have considered it only probable? How does that possibility affect your attitude towards those who disagree with you on that issue?
?
The passage warns against judging piety based on apparent acts of worship. Are there people in your life whom you have judged negatively because their visible deeds seemed insufficient? What hidden deeds might they have that you do not see?
?
If an issue is based on ijtihad and leaving its consideration does not incur sin, does that challenge how you prioritize your religious learning? What matters must be certain for you, and what are you willing to leave as probable?

The Scope of Tafḍīl: Outward and Inward, and Special Cases
Sanusi presents disagreements on the scope of tafḍīl and special cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the disagreements on whether tafḍīl applies to both outward and inward, and the special preference for those who died in the Prophet's lifetime, as well as the case of 'A'isha and Fatima.

Core Idea
Tafḍīl may be limited to outward qualities, and some Companions are preferred due to their time with the Prophet.

Having discussed whether tafḍīl is definitive, the scholars also debated its scope. Does preference refer to both apparent and hidden virtues, or only the apparent? Furthermore, is there a special preference for those Companions who witnessed the Prophet's lifetime? The passage also touches on the comparison between 'A'isha and Fatima, concluding with a unifying tribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on scope
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Identify the three sub-issues: outward vs inward, preference for those who died in the Prophet's lifetime, and the case of 'A'isha and Fatima.
The passage ends with a general tribute to all Companions.
2
Understand the outward vs inward debate
Note that al-Qadi supported both views but relied on the outward-only view, reasoning that the inward may be contrary to what we know.
3
Examine the preference for those who died in the Prophet's lifetime
A group held that Companions who died during the Prophet's life are better, citing a hadith. Ibn 'Abd al-Barr chose this view.
The hadith mentioned: 'I am a witness over these.'
4
Consider the 'A'isha-Fatima disagreement
There is disagreement between the merits of 'A'isha and Fatima, with each side using hadiths. Al-Ash'ari hesitated.
5
Reflect on the concluding tribute
Sanusi concludes by affirming that all Companions are noble and chosen, asking for benefit and gathering with them.
This emphasizes respect for all Companions despite disagreements.

What reason did al-Qadi give for relying on the view that tafḍīl is only in the outward?
A) Because the inward is always hidden from us.
B) Because it may be that the inward is contrary to what we have.
C) Because the hadiths only mention outward deeds.
D) Because he followed al-Ash'ari.

Key Takeaway
Scholars differed on the scope of tafḍīl, with some limiting it to outward deeds, and special consideration given to those who lived during the Prophet's time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own deeds, do you focus more on what is outwardly seen by others or on the inward state of your heart? The passage shows scholars debated whether tafḍīl is based on outward only. Which aspect do you neglect more, and what will you do today to check your inner sincerity?
?
The Companions differed in merit, but Sanusi reminds us they are all noble. Is there anyone you look down upon because of a perceived deficiency? How can you adopt the attitude of respecting all believers while acknowledging differences in virtue?
?
Al-Ash'ari hesitated and refrained from deciding on the superiority between Aisha and Fatima. Are you quick to judge matters where you lack certainty? What issue in your life requires you to pause and admit 'I do not know' instead of forming a strong opinion?
